Jamison Brereton

95 (921)
Puru╠Дravas and Urvas╠Б─▒╠Д
Dialogue between Pur┼лravas Aiс╕Нa and Urva┼Ы─л
18 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This very famous and much-discussed hymn contains the dialogue between the Apsaras Urva┼Ы─л and her discarded mortal husband Pur┼лravas. He accosts her on her journey (presumably back to her fellow Apsarases) and demands that they discuss what went wrong with their marriage (vs. 1). He reminisces about her beauty (vs. 3) and her good wifely ways (vs. 4), while she impatiently dismisses him (vs. 2) and provides her own view of her service as wife (vs. 5). The next verses (6тАУ11) primarily concern the crowd of Apsarases who attended Urva┼Ы─л when she gave birth to her and Pur┼лravasтАЩs son ─Аyu. Pur┼лravas evinces some jealousy about (as well as some physical attraction to) these females with whom he competed for Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs attention and to whom she is returning, while Urva┼Ы─л here implies that Pur┼лravas should have his mind on more manly matters than love, such as military protection (esp. vss. 7 and 11; see also the ironic vocative тАЬheroтАЭ in 5).
Urva┼Ы─л attempts to dismiss Pur┼лravas again (vs. 11). He tries another tack to keep her from leaving: how can she separate him from his loving son (vs. 12)тАФto which she briskly replies that sheтАЩll send him the kid, chillingly referred to in the neuter, back to him (vs. 12). The second half of this verse forms a ring with the second half of verse 2, her first speech: she seems thus to be trying to bring the conversation to a close. But Pur┼лravas raises the stakes: with masterfully expressed self-pity he then suggests that he may disappear or die (and wonтАЩt she be sorry then…?, vs. 14). Urva┼Ы─л wearily talks him out of it (vss. 15тАУ16). He tries one more time (vs. 17), using a grander and more solemn linguistic register. The hymn ends with a somewhat enigmatic summary verse (18) containing the godsтАЩ address to Pur┼лravas at the end of this affair. Because Pur┼лravasтАЩs connection with the immortal Apsaras (note that Apsarases are called тАЬimmortalтАЭ in vs. 9) was severed and his son was returned to him, the mortal, he is bound to death, and his offspring will relate to the gods as mortals do, by sacrifice. But he will nonetheless later receive a joyous afterlife in heaven. (It is noteworthy that this is the only occurrence of the word svarg├б тАЬheavenтАЭ in the R╠еgveda.)
One of the many extraordinary features of this brief masterpiece is the way it replicates the shifting emotional logic, the abrupt changes of tone and subject, and the twisting of the otherтАЩs words characteristic of a genuine marital quarrel of whatever era and culture, while presenting us with pictures of great beauty, however difficult the language is to interpret in many places. It is also uncompromising in its depiction of a resolute and hard-hearted female, unmoved by the abject pleas and emotional blackmail of her former lover who is still in love with her, anxious to return to her carefree life with her fellow Apsarases, and happy enough to abandon her child in order to get free.
There are several well-known later versions of this story. The ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa XI.5.1 embeds many of the R╠еgvedic verses into a prose narrative, which seems to have misunderstood, deliberately or not, several of the crucial verses. And one of the three surviving plays of the great Classical Sanskrit poet K─Бlid─Бsa is a much expanded treatment of the pairтАЩs love affair. No subsequent version can toler ate the radical portrait of the emotionally detached Urva┼Ы─л found in the R╠еgveda; in all cases the separation of the former lovers is not the result of the femaleтАЩs decision, but of a curse. In the ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, a creative misreading of verse 3тАФinvolv ing bleating pet lambs tied to a bedpost, a thunderstorm, and the provision that Urva┼Ы─л never see Pur┼лravas nakedтАФresults in Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs disappearance. In K─Бlid─БsaтАЩs play the curse has no connection to anything in the R╠еgvedic hymn: a love-besotted Urva┼Ы─л brings it on herself by uttering her beloved Pur┼лravasтАЩs name at the wrong time. (In both versions the portrayal of Pur┼лravas does retain his own passion for Urva┼Ы─л; in fact in K─Бlid─БsaтАЩs play he goes mad after she disappears and asks birds, beasts, and trees, in the late Middle Indo-Aryan language variety Apabhraс╣Г┼Ыa, about her whereabouts.) It is an interesting commentary on the changing fortunes of female figures that the hard edges of the R╠еgvedic Urva┼Ы─л must be softened to make her acceptable in later literature.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б) speaks). How indignant wife, with mind (relenting), stay awhile, let us now interchangediscourse. These, our secret thoughts, while unspoken, did not yield us happiness even at the last day.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Alegend: mitra and Varuс╣Зa, excited by the charms of ┼кrva┼Ы─л, gave birth to Agastya, pronouncing at the sametime an imprecation upon the nymph and condemning her to descend to earth and cohabit with a mortal. Iс╕╖─Б, aking, had gone out hunting with the sons of Manu. He reached a mountain where Um─Б, the daughter of themountain, with her attendant nymphs, was worshipping ┼Ъiva. In punishment for his intrusion, he was changedinto a woman. He prayed to ┼Ъiva and was restored to manhood; he was referred to Dev─л who allowed him to bealternately male and feminine le, six months at a time. in the latter condition Budha, the son of Soma, becameenamoured of her, and had a son by her, who was called Pur┼лrav─Б who became the king of Pratiс╣гс╣нh─Бna.Pur┼лrav─Б became enamoured of ┼кrva┼Ы─л, who became his mistress on condition that if he should be everaked in her sight, except in bed, she should return to heaven; he was also to take charge of two pet ramsbelonging to her. They lived together four years, when one night, hearing the bleating of the rams as they werebeing carried off by the gods, Pur┼лrav─Б sprang from the bed in pursuit, when a flash of lightning exhibited himto ┼кrva┼Ыi naked. She consequently left him and returned to heaven. Pur┼лrav─Б went in quest of her, andwandered aqbout like one distracted, until he finally discovered her sporting with fellow-nymphs. He implored herto return, but she refused, calling him by various opporbrious names, as horse, brute, and the like (vajra). Thisoccasions the dialogue of the s┼лkta, which contains an allusion to the past cohabitation of the king and thenymph and the unwillingness of the king to let his mistress depart. The legend is also related in the drama, theVikramorvas’I and in the ─Аdi parva of the Mah─Бbh─Бrata

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬWoe, wife! ThoughtfullyтАФstand still, fearsome woman!тАФ let us two now exchange words.
These thoughts, if unuttered, will not bring us joy even on a distant day.тАЭ

Griffith

Ho there, my consort! Stay, thou fierce-souled lady, and let us reason for a while together.
Such thoughts as these of ours, while yet unspoken in days gone by have never brought us comfort.

Geldner

Griffith

What am I now to do with this thy saying? I have gone from thee like the first of Mornings.
Pururavas, return thou to thy dwelling: I, like the wind, am difficult to capture.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). The arrow is not to be cast from the quiver for glory. I am no longer the impetuousdespoiler of the cattle (of the enemy), nor of their hundred-fold (riches). My prowess having lost its strength, (mymight) no longer flashes forth; (my warriors) the terrifiers (of the foe) hear not my shout in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬ…as an arrow from the quiver of beauty, a shot winning cows, as a charge winning hundreds.
Under the will of no man, she will keep flashing forth like (lightning); like a lamb its bleating, so are her tumultuous (tempests) displayed.тАЭ

Griffith

Like a shaft sent for glory from the quiver, or swift-steed winning cattle winning hundreds.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ыi). If, Uс╣гas, this ┼кrva┼Ы─л, offering food and wealth to her father-in-law, loves (her husband),she has gone from the neighbouring house to her husband’s home, where she loved (her lord), being delightednight and day by his embraces.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThrice a day, Pur┼лrav─Б, have you embraced me, you have loved me without a rival; I have followed(you) to your dwelling, you, hero, have been the sovereign of my person n.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thrice a day: an allusion perhaps, tothe three diurnal phases of the sun, his rising, culminating and setting, in which case Pur┼лrav─Б typifies the sun,and ┼кrva┼Ы─л either the wky or the day

Jamison Brereton

[Urva┼Ы─л:] тАЬThree times a day you used to pierced me with your rod, and you тАШfilled it upтАЩ [=had an erection] for me, who did not seek it.
Pur┼лravas, I followed your will. You were then the king of my body, you тАШhero.тАЩтАЭ

Griffith

Thrice in the day didst thou embrace thy consort, though coldly she received thy fond caresses.
To thy desires, Pururavas, I yielded: so wast thou king, O hero, of my body.

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). Suj┼лraс╣Зi, ┼Ъreс╣Зi, Sumna-─Бpi, Hradecakс╣гus, Granthin─л, and the swift-moving(┼кrva┼Ыi who arrived) they, decorated and purple-tinted, did not go first, they lowed like kine for protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬThe beautifully glowing rank (of Apsarases), friends in good favor, interlaced like a pondтАЩs-eye [=lotus], (always) on the moveтАФ
these flowed like reddish salves; like milk-cows they bellowed for beauty.тАЭ

Griffith

The maids Sujirni, Sreni, Sumne-api, Charanyu, Granthini, and Hradecaksus,-
These like red kine have hastened forth, the bright ones, and like milch-cows have lowed in emulation.

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ы─л). As soon as he was born the wives (of the gods) surrounded him, the spontaneouslyflowing rivers nourished him, for the gods reared you, Pur┼лrav─Б, for a mighty conflict, for the slaughter of theDasyus. (Nirukta, 3.47).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

themselves, strengthened him,
(just) as for great battle, for the smiting of Dasyus, the gods made you strong, Pur┼лravas.тАЭ

Griffith

While he was born the Dames sate down together, the Rivers with free kindness gave him nurture;
And then, Pururavas, the Gods increased thee for mighty battle, to destroy the Dasyus.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). When, becoming their companion, (Pur┼лrav─Б) the mortal associated with theseimmortal (nymphs) who had abandoned their bodies, they fled from me like a timid doe, like horses harnessed toa chariot.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬWhen I, a human, drew near to those nonhuman women when they were taking off their robes,
like a shy antelope they shied away from me, like horses that have brushed against a chariot.тАЭ

Griffith

When I, a mortal, wooed to mine embraces these heavenly nymphs who laid aside their raiment,
Like a scared snake they fled from me in terror, like chariot horses when the car has touched them.

Da ich Menschenskind mich bei diesen ├╝bermenschlichen Frauen anfreunden wollte, die ihr Gewand abgelegt haben, da scheuten sie vor mir wie eine br├╝nstige Gazelle, wie Pferde, die an den Wagen sto├Яen.

Grassmann

Als ich, der Mensch, jene ├╝bermenschlichen Weiber, die ihr Gewand fallen liessen, mit meinen Armen umschlang, da bebten sie vor mir zur├╝ck wie eine bebende Schlange, wie Rosse, die gegen den Wagen ausschlagen.

рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдЖрд╕реБ рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рд╕реБ рдЕрдкреНрд╕рд░рдГрд╕реБ рдорд░реНрддрдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ рдкреБрд░реВрд░рд╡рд╛рдГ рдирд┐рд╕реНрдкреГрдХреН рдирд┐рдГрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд╕реНрдкреГрд╢рдиреН рдХреНрд╖реЛрдгреАрднрд┐рдГ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрднрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рддреБрднрд┐рд░реНрди рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдВ рдкреГрдЩреНрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдХрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ ред рдирдХрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЪрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердГред рддрд╛рдГ рдЕрдкреНрд╕рд░рд╕рдГ рдЖрддрдпрдГ рдЖрддрд┐рднреВрддрд╛рд╕реНрддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рди рд╢реБрдореНрднрдд рди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕реЛ рди рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рдЗрд╡ рдХреНрд░реАрд│рдпрдГ рд╕рдВрдХреНрд░реАрдбрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджрдиреНрджрд╢рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджрдиреНрджрд╢реВрдХрд╛ рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рд░рд╛рддреНрдореАрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реГрдХреНрдХрд╛ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддрдГ ред рддреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдкрд▓реНрдпреЗрди рдзрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдВ рди рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рд░рдерд┐рдХрд╛рдп рддрджреНрд╡рджрд┐рддрд┐ рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рджреНрдмреНрд░реВрддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen a mortal mixing with these immortal nymphs has conversed with them with words and actions,they (becoming) ducks do not show their bodies, like plural yful horses champing (the bit).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ducks: they clean theirbodies like ducks;

Na = and (nak─Бraс╕е samucchay─Бrthaс╕е); not; like

Jamison Brereton

[Urva┼Ы─л:] тАЬWhen a mortal, going to caress immortal women, mingles (with their bodies) amid their cries, as if by his intentions,
like ducks they preen their own bodies, like horses playful and
constantly nipping.тАЭ

Griffith

When, loving these Immortal Ones, the mortal hath converse with the nymphs as they allow him.
Like swans they show the beauty of their bodies, like horses in their play they bite and nibble.

Geldner

Wenn der Sterbliche, nach diesen Unsterblichen l├╝stern, sich mit den Gesellschafterinnen einigt, wie es nach ihrem Sinn ist, dann macht eure Leiber sch├╢n wie die Wasserv├╢gel, wie Pferde spielend, die sich bei├Яen!

Grassmann

Wenn der Sterbliche mit den unsterblichen Weibern kosend sich mit den flutenden wie aus eigener Lust (?) mischt, dann schm├╝cken sie ihre Leiber wie Tauchenten, wie lustige Rosse einander beissend.

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрддреН-рдЖрд╕реБ-рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рд╕реБ) рдпрджрд╛-рдПрддрд╛рд╕реБ-рдЕрдореГрдд-рд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рд╕реБ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрд╖реБ (рдирд┐рд╕реНрдкреГрдХреН-рдорд░реНрддрдГ) рдирд┐рдпрдореЗрди рд╕реНрдкреГрд╣рд╛рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдЬрдирдГ рдкрддреНрдиреНрдпрдГ рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдГ (рдХреНрд╖реЛрдгреАрднрд┐рдГ-рдХреНрд░рддреБрднрд┐рдГ-рди рд╕рдореНрдкреГрдХреНрддреЗ) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рдордзреБрд░рд╢рдмреНрджреИрдГ тАЬрдХреНрд╖реБ рд╢рдмреНрджреЗтАЭ [рдЕрджрд╛рджрд┐реж] рддрддрдГ тАШрдирд┐рдГтАЩ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдп рдФрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рднреВрднрд╛рдЧреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ тАЬрдХреНрд╖реЛрдгрд┐рдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдирд╛рдотАЭ [рдирд┐рдШреж резредрез] рдЕрде рдЪ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ тАЬрдХреНрд░рддреБрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордирд╛рдотАЭ [рдирд┐рдШреж реиредрез] рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдХрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ (рддрд╛рдГ-рдЖрддрдпрдГ-рди) рддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдХрдкрд┐рдЮреНрдЬрд▓рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдг рдЗрд╡ рдордзреБрд░рдВ рднрд╛рд╖рдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ тАЬрдЕрдЬреНрдпрддрд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдЗрдиреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГтАЭ [рдЙрдгрд╛рджрд┐реж рекредрезрейрез рддрд┐рддреНрддрд┐рд░рд┐рднреЗрджрдГ рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] тАЬрддрдерд╛ рдЪ-рдЖрддрд┐рдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГтАЭ [рдпрдЬреБреж реирекредрейрек рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдкрддрдпреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдГ-рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рд╢реБрдореНрднрдд) рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢реЛрднрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрддреНрдорднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдорд░реНрдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рджрдиреНрджрд╢рд╛рдирд╛рдГ-рдХреНрд░реАрдбрдпрдГ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ-рди) рджрдВрд╢рдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджрдиреНрддрд╛рдиреН рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдХреНрд░реАрдбрдпрдиреНрддреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╢реЛрднрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ реерепрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ы─л) who shone like flashing lightning, bringing me the desirable dews (of heaven, hasappeared); a son able in act and friendly to man has been born; ┼кrva┼Ы─л has prolonged my lengthenedexistence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬShe who in her flight kept flashing like lightning, the watery (maiden) bringing me the delights of loveтАФ
(a son) belonging to men, nobly born, was born from the waterтАФ Urva┼Ы─л extends ─Аyu his lifetime long.тАЭ

Griffith

She who flashed brilliant as the falling lightning brought me delicious presents from the waters.
Now from the flood be born a strong young hero May Uruvasi prolong her life for ever

Geldner

Die wie ein fallender Blitz aufblitzte und mir Liebesg├╝sse brachte - aus der Feuchtigkeit ward ein mannhafter, edler Sohn geboren - Urvasi soll langes Leben haben.

Sie, welche wie ein herabst├╝rzender Blitz leuchtete, brachte mir die begehrungswerthe Feuchtigkeit, und aus dem Nass wurde geboren ein edler Knabe; langes Leben m├╢ge Urva├з─л verleihen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ы─л). you have been born thus to protect the earth; you have deposited this vigour in me;knowing (the future) I have instrumental ucted you (what to do) every day; you have not listened to me; why do you nowaddress me, neglectful (of my instrumental uction)?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Urva┼Ы─л:] тАЬYou were born just so: to afford protection. (But instead) you have exerted this force on me, Pur┼лravas.
I, knowing, instructed you on that very day. You did not listen to me. Why will you speak without profit?тАЭ

Griffith

Thy birth hath made me drink from earthly milch-kine: this power, Pururavas, hast thou vouchsafed me.
I knew, and, warned thee, on that day. Thou wouldst not hear me. What sayest thou, when naught avails thee?

Geldner

Du bist doch geboren, um hier Schutz zu bringen, und du hast diese Kraft an mich gewendet, Pururavas. Ich warnte dich, die Wissende, an dem gleichen Tage; du h├╢rtest nicht auf mich. Was willst du fruchtlos reden?

Grassmann

┬╗Du bist ja recht dazu geboren, um Schutz zu verleihen; diese Kraft hast du auch an mir erwiesen; ich, die ich’s weiss, unterwies dich an jenem Tage; du h├╢rtest nicht auf mich; was wirst du nun sagen, wenn dir der Genuss entzogen ist?┬л

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). When shall a son (born of you) claim me as a father, and crying, shed a tear onrecognizing (me)? What son shall sever husband and wife who are of one mind, now that the fire shines uponyour husband’s parents?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Fire shines: Agni is the fire in your heart, the embryo in the form of light, perhaps areference to the future son of ┼кrva┼Ы─л by pur┼лrav─Б

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬWhen will my begotten son seek his father? (When) will he let a tear roll like a wheel, on recognizing (him [=his father])?
Who keeps apart a married couple joined in mind as long as the fire will (still) blaze in (the house of) the parents-in-law?тАЭ

Griffith

When will the son be born and seek his father? Mourner-like, will he weep when first he knows him?
Who shall divide the accordant wife and husband, while fire is shining with thy consort’s parents?

Geldner

Wann wird der geborene Sohn seinen Vater suchen? Wie ein schreiendes Kind wird er Tr├дnen vergie├Яen, wann er Bescheid wei├Я. Wer trennt die eintr├дchtigen Ehegatten, da bei den Schwiegereltern noch das Hausfeuer hell luchtet?

Grassmann

Wann wird der Sohn, der geborene, nach dem Vater verlangen? wenn er’s erf├дhrt, wird er in der Erinnerung Thr├дnen vergiessen. Wer darf die gleichgesinnten Gatten trennen, so lange noch das Feuer bei den Schwieger├дltern leuchtet?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ы─л). Let me reply. (Your son) will shed tears, crying out and calling aloud when the expectedauspicious time arrives; I will send you that (child) which is yours in me, depart to your house, you cannot,simpleton, detain me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Auspicious time: adhye = adhyate vast┼лni, the expected thing; adhye ┼Ыivayai: let meforbid him as he sheds tears (i.e., I will forbid him to shed tears); calling out he shall not weep for the fortunatesolicitude (of his father). Pur┼лrav─Б seems to urge as an argument for ┼кrva┼Ы─л’s return that the son expectedto be born (or, already born?) will long for his father, and, if separated from him, will weep, to which ┼кrva┼Ы─лrepies that the son will not weep because she will send him to Pur┼лrav─Б; which is yours in me: i.e., which youhave plural ced in my womb

That which is thine, between us, will I send thee. Go home again, thou fool;.thou hast not won me.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). (Your husband) who sports with you may now depart, never to return, (depart) toproceed to a distant region. Either let him sleep upon the lap of Nirс╣Ыti, or let the swift-moving wolves devour hiс╣ГтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let him sleep: i.e., let him die; Nirс╣Ыti being either the earth or the goddess of ill

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬAnd if the godsтАЩ pet should fly away today, never to return, to go to the most distant distance …
Then he might lie in the lap of Dissolution. Then again the ravening wolves might eat him…тАЭ

Griffith

Thy lover shall flee forth this day for ever, to seek, without return, the farthest distance.
Then let his bed be in Destruction’s bosom, and there let fierce rapacious wolves devour him.

With women there can be no lasting friendship: hearts of hyenas are the hearts of women.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen changed in form I wandered among mortals. I dwelt (with them) four delightful years. I ate oncea day a small quantity of butter; satisfied with that I now depart.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Delightful years: praramayitr─лс╕е = p┼лrayitr─лс╕е,i.e., satisfying; or, r─Бtr─лс╕е: I spent my nights there during four years

Jamison Brereton

[Urva┼Ы─л:] тАЬWhen in different form I roamed among mortals and spent the nights (with you?) for four autumns,
once a day I ate a drop of ghee. Just from that I continue to be sated now.тАЭ

Griffith

When amid men in altered shape I sojourned, and through four autumns spent the nights among them,
I tasted once a day a drop of butter; and even now with that am I am contented.

Geldner

Als ich in anderer Gestalt unter den Sterblichen wandelte, vier Jahre lang alle N├дchte bei dir wohnte, da geno├Я ich einmal des Tags einen Tropfen Schmalz. Davon bin ich noch jetzt ges├дttigt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Pur┼лrav─Б). I, Vasiс╣гс╣нha, bring under subjection ┼кrva┼Ы─л who fills the firmament (with lustre) andmeasures out the rain. May (Pur┼лrav─Б), the bestower of the auspicious rite, abide near you; come back– myheart is burning.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vasiс╣гс╣нha: an epithet, pre-eminently the giver of dwellings

Jamison Brereton

[Pur┼лravas:] тАЬShe who fills the midspace, who is the measurer of the dusky realm, Urva┼Ы─лтАФI, the best (of men?), seek to bring her under my sway.
Since the granting of a good deed will stand you in good stead, turn back: my heart is scorched.тАЭ

Griffith

I, her best love, call Urvasi to meet me, her who fills air and measures out the region.
Let the gift brought by piety approach thee. Turn thou to me again: my heart is troubled.

Geldner

Die die L├╝fte erf├╝llende, den Raum durchmessende Urvasi locke ich her, ihr Liebster: Auf da├Я der Lohn der Guttat dir zuteil werde, kehre um, mein Herz verzehrt sich!

Grassmann

Die Urva├з─л, die die Luft erf├╝llt, und den Raum durchmisst, verehre ich, der trefflichste; dich m├╢ge erreichen, was die Fr├╢mmigkeit darbringt; o kehre wieder, mein Herz wird gequ├дlt.

English translation:

тАЬ(┼кrva┼Ы─л). These gods said to you, Aiс╕╖a, since you are indeed subject to death, let your progenypropitiate your gods with oblations, you shall rejoice (with me) in heaven.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Thus these gods here say to you, Aiс╕Нa [=Pur┼лravas]: тАЬAs it (turned out) this way, you have a bond to death.
Your progeny will sacrifice to the gods with an oblation, but you will also rejoice in heaven.тАЭ

Griffith

Thus speak these Gods to thee, O son of Ila: As death hath verily got thee for his subject,
Thy sons shall serve the Gods with their oblation, and thou, moreover, shalt rejoice in Svarga.
